     <p>
      <i>
       <b>
        The Hobbit: The Battle of the Five Armies
       </b>
      </i>
      is a 2014
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epic_fantasy" title="Epic fantasy">
       epic fantasy
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Adventure_film" title="Adventure film">
       adventure film
      </a>
      , directed by
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson" title="Peter Jackson">
       Peter Jackson
      </a>
      and written by Jackson,
      <a href="/wiki/Fran_Walsh" title="Fran Walsh">
       Fran Walsh
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Philippa_Boyens" title="Philippa Boyens">
       Philippa Boyens
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_del_Toro" title="Guillermo del Toro">
       Guillermo del Toro
      </a>
      . It is the third and final installment in Peter Jackson's
      <a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit_(film_series)" title="The Hobbit (film series)">
       three-part film adaptation
      </a>
      based on the novel
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit" title="The Hobbit">
        The Hobbit
       </a>
      </i>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/J._R._R._Tolkien" title="J. R. R. Tolkien">
       J. R. R. Tolkien
      </a>
      , following
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit:_An_Unexpected_Journey" title="The Hobbit: An Unexpected Journey">
        An Unexpected Journey
       </a>
      </i>
      (2012) and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit:_The_Desolation_of_Smaug" title="The Hobbit: The Desolation of Smaug">
        The Desolation of Smaug
       </a>
      </i>
      (2013), and together they act as a
      <a href="/wiki/Prequel" title="Prequel">
       prequel
      </a>
      to Jackson's
      <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)" title="The Lord of the Rings (film series)">
       <i>
        The Lord of the Rings
       </i>
       film trilogy
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Produced by
      <a href="/wiki/New_Line_Cinema" title="New Line Cinema">
       New Line Cinema
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">
       Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/WingNut_Films" title="WingNut Films">
       WingNut Films
      </a>
      , and distributed by
      <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">
       Warner Bros.
      </a>
      Pictures,
      <i>
       The Battle of the Five Armies
      </i>
      was released on 11 December 2014 in New Zealand, 12 December 2014 in the United Kingdom and on 17 December 2014 in the United States.
     </p>
     <p>
      It stars
      <a href="/wiki/Martin_Freeman" title="Martin Freeman">
       Martin Freeman
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen" title="Ian McKellen">
       Ian McKellen
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Armitage_(actor)" title="Richard Armitage (actor)">
       Richard Armitage
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Evangeline_Lilly" title="Evangeline Lilly">
       Evangeline Lilly
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Lee_Pace" title="Lee Pace">
       Lee Pace
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Luke_Evans_(actor)" title="Luke Evans (actor)">
       Luke Evans
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Benedict_Cumberbatch" title="Benedict Cumberbatch">
       Benedict Cumberbatch
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ken_Stott" title="Ken Stott">
       Ken Stott
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/James_Nesbitt" title="James Nesbitt">
       James Nesbitt
      </a>
      . It also features
      <a href="/wiki/Cate_Blanchett" title="Cate Blanchett">
       Cate Blanchett
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ian_Holm" title="Ian Holm">
       Ian Holm
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Lee" title="Christopher Lee">
       Christopher Lee
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Weaving" title="Hugo Weaving">
       Hugo Weaving
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Bloom" title="Orlando Bloom">
       Orlando Bloom
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The film was a box office success, grossing over $955 million worldwide, surpassing both
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Fellowship of the Ring">
        The Fellowship of the Ring
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Two_Towers" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers">
        The Two Towers
       </a>
      </i>
      nominally, making it the
      <a href="/wiki/2014_in_film" title="2014 in film">
       second highest-grossing film of 2014
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">
       29th highest-grossing film of all time
      </a>
      . At the
      <a href="/wiki/87th_Academy_Awards" title="87th Academy Awards">
       87th Academy Awards
      </a>
      , the film received a nomination for
      <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound_Editing" title="Academy Award for Best Sound Editing">
       Best Sound Editing
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">
       Plot
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Hobbit:_The_Battle_of_the_Five_Armies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Bilbo_Baggins" title="Bilbo Baggins">
       Bilbo
      </a>
      and the Dwarves watch from the
      <a href="/wiki/Lonely_Mountain" title="Lonely Mountain">
       Lonely Mountain
      </a>
      as the dragon
      <a href="/wiki/Smaug" title="Smaug">
       Smaug
      </a>
      attacks
      <a href="/wiki/Esgaroth" title="Esgaroth">
       Laketown
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Bard_the_Bowman" title="Bard the Bowman">
       Bard the Bowman
      </a>
      manages to break out of prison, fights Smaug, and eventually kills him with the black arrow given to him by his son
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_kings_of_Dale" title="List of kings of Dale">
       Bain
      </a>
      . Smaug's falling body crushes the fleeing Master of Laketown, along with his cronies, who were escaping Laketown on a boat with the town's gold. Bard becomes the new leader of the Laketown people as they seek refuge in the ruins of Dale, while
      <a href="/wiki/Legolas" title="Legolas">
       Legolas
      </a>
      travels to investigate
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_minor_places_in_Middle-earth#Mount_Gundabad" title="List of minor places in Middle-earth">
       Mount Gundabad
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Tauriel" title="Tauriel">
       Tauriel
      </a>
      . Thorin, now struck with "dragon sickness", searches obsessively for the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arkenstone" title="Arkenstone">
       Arkenstone
      </a>
      , which was stolen earlier from Smaug by Bilbo. Bilbo learns from Balin that it would be best if the Arkenstone remained hidden from Thorin, who orders the entrance of the Lonely Mountain to be sealed off.
     </p>
     <p>
      Meanwhile,
      <a href="/wiki/Galadriel" title="Galadriel">
       Galadriel
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Elrond" title="Elrond">
       Elrond
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Saruman" title="Saruman">
       Saruman
      </a>
      arrive at
      <a href="/wiki/Dol_Guldur" title="Dol Guldur">
       Dol Guldur
      </a>
      and free
      <a href="/wiki/Gandalf" title="Gandalf">
       Gandalf
      </a>
      , sending him to safety with
      <a href="/wiki/Radagast" title="Radagast">
       Radagast
      </a>
      . They battle and defeat the
      <a href="/wiki/Nazg%C3%BBl" title="Nazgl">
       Nazgl
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Sauron" title="Sauron">
       Sauron
      </a>
      himself, banishing them to the East.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azog" title="Azog">
       Azog
      </a>
      , marching on Erebor with his vast Orc army, sends
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolg" title="Bolg">
       Bolg
      </a>
      to Gundabad to summon their second army. Legolas and Tauriel witness the march of Bolg's army, bolstered by Goblins and giant bats.
     </p>
     <p>
      While Bard and the Laketown survivors shelter in Dale,
      <a href="/wiki/Thranduil" title="Thranduil">
       Thranduil
      </a>
      arrives with an elf army, supplies and aid, and forms an alliance with Bard, wishing to claim an elven necklace of white gems from the Mountain. Bard attempts to negotiate and reason with Thorin to avoid war, but the dwarf refuses to cooperate. After Gandalf arrives at Dale to warn Bard and Thranduil of the Orc army on the way, Bilbo sneaks out of Erebor to hand the Arkenstone over to Thranduil and Bard. When Bard and Thranduil's armies gather at the gates of Erebor, offering to trade the Arkenstone for Thranduil's gems and Laketown's share of the gold, Thorin nearly kills Bilbo in a furious rage. After Gandalf forces Thorin to release Bilbo, the arrival of Thorin's cousin
      <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1in_II_Ironfoot" title="Din II Ironfoot">
       Din
      </a>
      with his Dwarf army worsens matters. A battle of Dwarves against Elves and Men is imminent, when
      <a href="/wiki/Wereworms" title="Wereworms">
       Wereworms
      </a>
      emerge from the ground releasing Azog's army from their tunnels. With the Orcs outnumbering Dain's army, Thranduil and Bard's forces, along with Gandalf and Bilbo, join the battle as some of the Orcs attack Dale.
     </p>
     <p>
      Inside Erebor, initially refusing to fight, Thorin suffers a hallucination before regaining his sanity and leading his company into battle. While the other dwarves of the company aid Dain's forces, Thorin rides towards
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ravenhill_(Middle-earth)" title="Ravenhill (Middle-earth)">
       Ravenhill
      </a>
      with Dwalin, Fili and Kili to kill Azog and force the Orcs to retreat. Meanwhile, after being banished by Thranduil, Tauriel leaves with Legolas to warn the dwarves of Bolg's approaching army; Bilbo follows them using his invisibility ring. Thorin sends Fli and Kli to scout, but they are captured by orcs. Bilbo and the elves arrive too late as Fli is executed by Azog. Kli, who is hiding underneath the cliff, sees his brother's body dropping down and attacks some Orcs in a fit of rage. As Thorin battles Azog to avenge Fili, Bolg knocks Bilbo unconscious, overpowers Tauriel and then kills Kili who had come to her aid. After Legolas kills Bolg, the
      <a href="/wiki/Eagle_(Middle-earth)" title="Eagle (Middle-earth)">
       Great Eagles
      </a>
      arrive with Radagast and
      <a href="/wiki/Beorn" title="Beorn">
       Beorn
      </a>
      , and the Orc armies are finally destroyed.
     </p>
     <p>
      Bilbo regains consciousness and finds that Azog has been killed by Thorin, who makes peace with him before succumbing to his own injuries. On Thranduil's suggestion, Legolas leaves to meet with a young Dunedain ranger going by the name "Strider" (
      <a href="/wiki/Aragorn" title="Aragorn">
       Aragorn
      </a>
      ). Grieved by the deaths of Thorin, Fili, and Kili, the people of Laketown, the elves, and the dwarves bury them inside the tombs of Erebor. As a result, Dain is crowned King Under the Mountain, the citizens of Laketown are given the riches promised to them by Thorin, and Dain returns to the elves the white elven gems that King Thror had stolen from them years ago.
     </p>
     <p>
      Following these events, Bilbo bids farewell to the remaining members of Thorin's company and journeys home to the Shire with Gandalf. As the two part on the outskirts of the Shire, Gandalf admits his knowledge of Bilbo's ring and cautions him against using it. Bilbo returns to Bag End to find his belongings being
      <a href="/wiki/Estate_sale" title="Estate sale">
       auctioned off
      </a>
      by relatives' family because he was
      <a href="/wiki/Declared_death_in_absentia" title="Declared death in absentia">
       presumed dead
      </a>
      . He aborts the sale but finds his home has been almost totally pillaged.
     </p>
     <p>
      Sixty years later, Bilbo receives a visit from Gandalf and runs out to greet him, thus setting in motion the events of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Fellowship of the Ring">
        The Fellowship of the Ring
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>

         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Billy_Connolly" title="Billy Connolly">
         Billy Connolly
        </a>
        as
        <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1in_II_Ironfoot" title="Din II Ironfoot">
         Din
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Mikael_Persbrandt" title="Mikael Persbrandt">
         Mikael Persbrandt
        </a>
        as
        <a href="/wiki/Beorn" title="Beorn">
         Beorn
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Fry" title="Stephen Fry">
         Stephen Fry
        </a>
        as the Master of
        <a href="/wiki/Esgaroth" title="Esgaroth">
         Laketown
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Gage" title="Ryan Gage">
         Ryan Gage
        </a>
        as
        <a href="/wiki/List_of_original_characters_in_The_Hobbit_film_series#Men" title="List of original characters in The Hobbit film series">
         Alfrid Lickspittle
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Mark_Mitchinson" title="Mark Mitchinson">
         Mark Mitchinson
        </a>
        as
        <a href="/wiki/List_of_original_characters_in_The_Hobbit_film_series#Men" title="List of original characters in The Hobbit film series">
         Braga
        </a>
       </li>

        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Bell_(child_actor)" title="John Bell (child actor)">
         John Bell
        </a>
        as
        <a href="/wiki/List_of_kings_of_Dale" title="List of kings of Dale">
         Bain
        </a>
       </li>

        Peggy and Mary Nesbitt as
        <a href="/wiki/List_of_original_characters_in_The_Hobbit_film_series#Tilda_and_Sigrid" title="List of original characters in The Hobbit film series">
         Tilda and Sigrid
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Simon London as
        <a href="/wiki/List_of_original_characters_in_The_Hobbit_film_series#Elves" title="List of original characters in The Hobbit film series">
         Feren
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
     </div>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Production">
       Production
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Hobbit:_The_Battle_of_the_Five_Armies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit_(film_series)#Development" title="The Hobbit (film series)">
       The Hobbit (film series)  Development
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      <i>
       The Hobbit
      </i>
      was originally envisioned as a two-part film, but Jackson confirmed plans for a third film on 30 July 2012, turning his adaptation of
      <i>
       The Hobbit
      </i>
      into a trilogy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR30712_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-THR30712-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PJFB30712_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-PJFB30712-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to Jackson, the third film would contain the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Five_Armies" title="Battle of the Five Armies">
       Battle of the Five Armies
      </a>
      and make extensive use of the appendices that Tolkien wrote to expand the story of Middle-Earth (published in the back of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Return_of_the_King" title="The Return of the King">
        The Return of the King
       </a>
      </i>
      ). Jackson also stated that while the third film will largely make use of footage originally shot for the first and second films, it would require additional filming as well.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The third film was titled
      <i>
       There and Back Again
      </i>
      in August 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McClintock_11-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-McClintock-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In April 2014, Jackson changed the title of the film to
      <i>
       The Battle of the Five Armies
      </i>
      as he thought the new title better suited the situation of the film.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian1_12-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Guardian1-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He stated on his
      <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">
       Facebook
      </a>
      page, "
      <i>
       There and Back Again
      </i>
      felt like the right name for the second of a two film telling of the quest to reclaim Erebor, when Bilbo's arrival there, and departure, were both contained within the second film. But with three movies, it suddenly felt misplacedafter all, Bilbo has already arrived 'there' in the
      <i>
       Desolation of Smaug
      </i>
      ."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metro_13-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Metro-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Shaun Gunner, the chairman of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Tolkien_Society" title="The Tolkien Society">
       The Tolkien Society
      </a>
      , supported the decision: "
      <i>
       The Battle of the Five Armies
      </i>
      much better captures the focus of the film but also more accurately channels the essence of the story."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Score">
       Score
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Hobbit:_The_Battle_of_the_Five_Armies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Score">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Music_of_The_Hobbit_film_series#The_Battle_of_the_Five_Armies" title="Music of The Hobbit film series">
       Music of The Hobbit film series  The Battle of the Five Armies
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      As with all the previous films,
      <a href="/wiki/Howard_Shore" title="Howard Shore">
       Howard Shore
      </a>
      has composed the score.
      <a href="/wiki/Billy_Boyd_(actor)" title="Billy Boyd (actor)">
       Billy Boyd
      </a>
      , who played
      <a href="/wiki/Peregrin_Took" title="Peregrin Took">
       Peregrin Took
      </a>
      in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)" title="The Lord of the Rings (film series)">
        The Lord of the Rings
       </a>
      </i>
      , wrote and recorded the song "The Last Goodbye" to be played over the end credits of the film.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Release">
       Release
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Hobbit:_The_Battle_of_the_Five_Armies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Release">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">
       Marketing
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Hobbit:_The_Battle_of_the_Five_Armies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Marketing">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      A teaser trailer for the film was released on 28 July 2014 attached to
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Guardians_of_the_Galaxy_(film)" title="Guardians of the Galaxy (film)">
        Guardians of the Galaxy
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Into_the_Storm_(2014_film)" title="Into the Storm (2014 film)">
        Into the Storm
       </a>
      </i>
      , and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/If_I_Stay_(film)" title="If I Stay (film)">
        If I Stay
       </a>
      </i>
      . The second theatrical trailer was released on 6 November 2014 attached to
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Interstellar_(film)" title="Interstellar (film)">
        Interstellar
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Hunger_Games:_Mockingjay_%E2%80%93_Part_1" title="The Hunger Games: Mockingjay  Part 1">
        The Hunger Games: Mockingjay  Part 1
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      To promote the film's release, Wellington-based
      <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
       association football
      </a>
      club,
      <a href="/wiki/Wellington_Phoenix_FC" title="Wellington Phoenix FC">
       Wellington Phoenix
      </a>
      , wore a special designed jersey to commemorate the opening of
      <i>
       The Hobbit: The Battle of Five Armies
      </i>
      . The custom, film-themed jersey was worn only once, on 13 December 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the film's Japanese release on 13 December, Warner Bros. collaborated with mobile gaming company A-Lim to bring Bilbo, Gandalf, and Legolas into the game
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Brave_Frontier" title="Brave Frontier">
        Brave Frontier
       </a>
      </i>
      at the end of December as Vortex Dungeon units. The campaign only runs until February 2015.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Smaug made a guest appearance, animated by WETA and voiced again by Cumberbatch, on the satire show
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Colbert_Report" title="The Colbert Report">
        The Colbert Report
       </a>
      </i>
      on December 12, 2014 to promote the film.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Theatrical_release">
       Theatrical release
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Hobbit:_The_Battle_of_the_Five_Armies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Theatrical release">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The world premiere of
      <i>
       The Hobbit: The Battle of the Five Armies
      </i>
      was held in
      <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">
       London
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Square" title="Leicester Square">
       Leicester Square
      </a>
      on 1 December 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The film opened in theatres on 11 December 2014 in New Zealand, on 12 December in the United Kingdom and on 17 December in the United States. Warner Bros released the film on 18 December 2014 in Greece and 26 December in Australia.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EmpireOnline1_6-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-EmpireOnline1-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LATimes_25-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-LATimes-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The film was released in China on January 23, 2015.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chinarelease_26-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Chinarelease-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">
       Home media
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Hobbit:_The_Battle_of_the_Five_Armies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Home media">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <i>
       The Hobbit: The Battle of the Five Armies
      </i>
      was released on March 6, 2015 on Digital Release from digital retailers. The DVD and Blu-ray were released on March 24, 2015 in the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It topped the home video sales chart in its opening week.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      An Extended Edition of the film is scheduled for release in November 2015 and will be 30 minutes longer than the theatrical cut.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <span id="Reception">
      </span>
     </p>

      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>

       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-style ambox-overly_detailed" role="presentation">

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">
       Box office
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Hobbit:_The_Battle_of_the_Five_Armies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Box office">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <i>
       The Hobbit: The Battle of the Five Armies
      </i>
      grossed a worldwide total of $955.1 million. Calculating in all expenses,
      <a href="/wiki/Deadline.com" title="Deadline.com">
       Deadline.com
      </a>
      estimated that the film made a profit of $103.38 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Worldwide, it is the
      <a href="/wiki/2014_in_film" title="2014 in film">
       second highest-grossing film of 2014
      </a>
      behind
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Transformers:_Age_of_Extinction" title="Transformers: Age of Extinction">
        Transformers: Age of Extinction
       </a>
      </i>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">
       28th highest-grossing film of all time
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Its grosses exceeded its estimated $250 million production cost 12 days after its release.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The film failed to earn $1 billion at the box office despite various pundits projecting it to reach that milestone.
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">
        The Hollywood Reporter
       </a>
      </i>
      said that
      <i>
       The Battle of the Five Armies
      </i>
      was unlikely to gross $1 billion worldwide due to "plunging exchange rates around the globe" witnessed that year and that Warner Bros. and MGM ultimately would take in nearly $90 million less than expected due to rising dollar and plunging foreign currencies.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, despite this failure,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">
        Forbes
       </a>
      </i>
      has declared the trilogy "an unmitigated financial grand-slam for all parties."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_and_Canada">
       United States and Canada
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Hobbit:_The_Battle_of_the_Five_Armies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: United States and Canada">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      In the U.S. and Canada, it is the lowest grossing of the three films in
      <i>
       The Hobbit
      </i>
      franchise,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and also the lowest grossing of the six Middle-earth adaptations,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but the sixth highest-grossing film of 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It opened on Tuesday, December 16, 2014 at 7 p.m across 3,100 theaters and widened to 3,875 theaters the following day.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dead_42-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dead-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It earned $11.2 million from Tuesday late-night shows, which was the second highest of 2014, matching the record previously set by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Guardians_of_the_Galaxy_(film)" title="Guardians of the Galaxy (film)">
        Guardians of the Galaxy
       </a>
      </i>
      and both behind
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Hunger_Games:_Mockingjay_%E2%80%93_Part_1" title="The Hunger Games: Mockingjay  Part 1">
        The Hunger Games: Mockingjay  Part 1
       </a>
      </i>
      ($17 million).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dead_42-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dead-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It then topped the box office on its opening day (Wednesday, December 17, 2014), earning $24.5 million (including previews),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estimate2_46-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-estimate2-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      which was the third highest Middle-earth adaptation Wednesday opening behind the Wednesday openings of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Return_of_the_King" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Return of the King">
        The Lord of the Rings: The Return of the King
       </a>
      </i>
      ($34.5 million) and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Two_Towers" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers">
        The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers
       </a>
      </i>
      ($26.2 million).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estimate1_48-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-estimate1-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In total, the film earned $54,724,334 in its traditional three-day opening and $89,131,544 over its five-day course making it the second biggest five-day opening in the
      <i>
       Hobbit
      </i>
      trilogy, beating the $86.1 million five-day opening gross of
      <i>
       The Desolation of Smaug
      </i>
      , but still behind
      <i>
       An Unexpected Journey'
      </i>
      s $100.2 million five-day opening. However, on a three-day basis the film underperformed expectations and fell short of its predecessors.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM_51-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BOM-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The film set a December
      <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">
       IMAX
      </a>
      opening record with $13.4 million (previously held by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Mission:_Impossible_%E2%80%93_Ghost_Protocol" title="Mission: Impossible  Ghost Protocol">
        Mission: Impossible  Ghost Protocol
       </a>
      </i>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMAX_52-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-IMAX-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      3D accounted for 49% of the total gross while IMAX generated 15% or $13.4 million over five days, and $7.4 million over three days, and premium large format screens comprised 8% of the total opening weekend gross with $7.2 million from 396 theaters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dead_42-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dead-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM_51-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-BOM-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The film passed the $100 million mark on December 23, 2014  on its seventh day.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It became the third film of 2014 to earn $100 million in just under a week following
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lionsgate" title="Lionsgate">
       Lionsgate
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       The Hunger Games: Mockingjay  Part 1
      </i>
      ($168.7 million in its opening week) and
      <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Motion_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures">
       Disney
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Studios" title="Marvel Studios">
       Marvel
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       Guardians of the Galaxy
      </i>
      ($134.4 million in its first week).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was in first place at the North American box office for three consecutive weekends despite facing competition from numerous new releases each weekend,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nancy_Tartaglione_55-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Nancy_Tartaglione-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but was finally overtaken by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Taken_3" title="Taken 3">
        Taken 3
       </a>
      </i>
      in its fourth weekend.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boom_58-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-boom-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_territories">
       Other territories
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Hobbit:_The_Battle_of_the_Five_Armies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Other territories">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The film began its international roll-out a week prior to its wide North American release.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HUGE_59-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HUGE-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It opened Wednesday, December 10, 2014 in 11 European markets, earning $11.3 million and December 11, 2014 in 17 additional markets, earning $13.7 million, for a two day total of $26.6 million and topped the charts in each of the territories.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HUGE_59-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HUGE-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Through Sunday, December 14, 2015, it had an openening weekend total of $122.2 million from 37 countries in 15,395 screens
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BO_62-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BO-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadline_63-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Deadline-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      topping the box office and outperforming the previous two installments on a local currency and admissions basis.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadline_63-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Deadline-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      71% of the total gross ($86.7 million) came from 3D showings.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadline_63-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Deadline-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the overseas opening weekend was still lower than the openings of
      <i>
       An Unexpected Journey
      </i>
      ($138 million)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxoffice_64-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-boxoffice-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <i>
       The Desolation of Smaug
      </i>
      ($135.4 million)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
       both on a dollar basis. It set a December IMAX opening record with $6.4 million across 160 IMAX screens, previously held by
      <i>
       An Unexpected Journey
      </i>
      with $5.03 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadline_63-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Deadline-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The film opened to an additional 59 countries in its second weekend and earned $109 million from 19,315 screens still holding the top spot and fell gradually by 13% as a result of facing minor competitions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMAX_52-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-IMAX-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In its third weekend the film added a further $89 million abroad, remaining at No. 1.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-update_67-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-update-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was in first place at the box office outside North America for four consecutive weekends
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-500million_68-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-500million-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and five in total.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-China_69-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-China-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In Australia, the film was released on December 26, 2014 and set an opening day record with $5.59 million, which is the biggest of 2014, the second biggest
      <a href="/wiki/Boxing_Day" title="Boxing Day">
       Boxing Day
      </a>
      gross, and the fourth biggest ever in Australia
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      behind
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows  Part 2">
        Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows  Part 2
       </a>
      </i>
      ($7.092 million),
      <i>
       The Avengers
      </i>
      ($6.004 million) and
      <i>
       The Hobbit: The Desolation of Smaug
      </i>
      ($5.9 million).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It went on to earn $10.1 million in its opening weekend.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-update_67-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-update-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The film set an all time opening record for Warner Bros. in China where it earned $49.84 million in its opening weekend (a record previously held by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Rim_(film)" title="Pacific Rim (film)">
        Pacific Rim
       </a>
      </i>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-China_69-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-China-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      IMAX generated $6.8 million of the total gross which is the second-highest IMAX three day gross in China behind
      <i>
       Transformers: Age of Extinction
      </i>
      's $10 million gross.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-China_69-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-China-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The film achieved numerous records in international markets during its opening weekend. It set an all-time Warner Bros. opening record in Russia ($13.75 million),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BO_62-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-BO-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in Argentina ($2.1 million),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-500million_68-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-500million-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in Sweden and Finland.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BO_62-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-BO-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It also set a 2014 opening record in Germany ($20.5 million),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BO_62-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-BO-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      France ($15.05 million)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BO_62-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-BO-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in Spain ($6.3 million).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BO2_74-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BO2-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It also had the best Middle-earth saga opening in the UK ($15.2 million)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BO_62-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-BO-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in Mexico ($6.3 million).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BO_62-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-BO-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In Brazil, the film scored the second biggest Warner Bros. opening of all time with $6.8 million (behind
      <i>
       Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows - Part 2
      </i>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BO_62-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-BO-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other high openings were recorded in Korea ($10.4 million), Poland ($5.6 million), Italy ($5.6 million), Malaysia ($3 million) and Taiwan ($2.75 million).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BO2_74-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-BO2-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-update_67-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-update-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In total earnings, its largest markets are China ($121.7 million), UK, Ireland and Malta ($61.3 million) and Australia ($27 million).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_response">
       Critical response
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Hobbit:_The_Battle_of_the_Five_Armies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Critical response">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">
       MTV
      </a>
      reported that reviews for
      <i>
       The Hobbit: The Battle of the Five Armies
      </i>
      were "generally positive" with critics praising the film "for its energy, shorter running time and satisfying closure."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to
      <a href="/wiki/International_Business_Times" title="International Business Times">
       IBT
      </a>
      , reviews for the film were mostly positive, with critics "praising director Peter Jackson's effort at transforming J.R.R Tolkien's fantasy novel into an epic adventure film trilogy."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to
      <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">
       CBS News
      </a>
      , critics said the film "will satisfy" fans but "otherwise, it may be worth waiting until it's available to rent."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">
        Los Angeles Times
       </a>
      </i>
      said the critical consensus was that the film is "a flawed but fitting finale to the
      <i>
       Hobbit
      </i>
      trilogy."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Review_aggregator" title="Review aggregator">
       review aggregator
      </a>
      website
      <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">
       Rotten Tomatoes
      </a>
      reported a 61% approval rating with an average rating of 6.3/10 based on 219 reviews. The website's consensus reads, "Though somewhat overwhelmed by its own spectacle, The Hobbit: The Battle of the Five Armies ends Peter Jackson's second Middle-earth trilogy on a reasonably satisfying note."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The film also holds a
      <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">
       Metacritic
      </a>
      score of 59 out of 100, based on 45 critics, indicating "mixed or average reviews".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/CinemaScore" title="CinemaScore">
       CinemaScore
      </a>
      polls conducted during the opening weekend, cinema audiences gave the film an average grade of "A-" on an A+ to F scale.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM_51-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-BOM-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Scott Foundas of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">
        Variety
       </a>
      </i>
      said, "The result is at once the trilogy's most engrossing episode, its most expeditious (at a comparatively lean 144 minutes) and also its darkest - both visually and in terms of the forces that stir in the hearts of men, dwarves and orcs alike."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Todd McCarthy of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">
        The Hollywood Reporter
       </a>
      </i>
      said, "After six films, 13 years and 1031 minutes of accumulated running time, Peter Jackson has concluded his massively remunerative genuflection at the altar of J.R.R. Tolkien with a film that may be the most purely entertaining of any in the collection."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Andrew Pulver of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">
        The Guardian
       </a>
      </i>
      said, "This film is a fitting cap to an extended series that, if nothing else, has transformed Tolkien's place in the wider culture."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Chris Tilly from
      <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">
       IGN Movies
      </a>
      said, "There's a little too much padding in the final
      <i>
       Hobbit
      </i>
      flick, and the best sequence is without doubt the film's first. But the central battle is indeed spectacular, and as 'The Age of Orc' approaches, it rounds out this particular story in stirring and emotional fashion."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Russell Baillie of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_New_Zealand_Herald" title="The New Zealand Herald">
        The New Zealand Herald
       </a>
      </i>
      said
      <i>
       The Hobbit: The Battle of the Five Armies
      </i>
      is "something less than the supposed 'defining chapter' of Jackson's time in Middle-earth as it's been billed. But action-wise, it certainly goes out with a very pleasing bang."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Conversely, Inkoo Kang of
      <a href="/wiki/TheWrap" title="TheWrap">
       TheWrap
      </a>
      said, "The 144-minute running time showcases Jackson's worst tendencies: eons-long battle scenes, sloppy and abrupt resolutions, portentous romances, off-rhythm comic timing, and, newly in this case, patience-testing fan service."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Tim Robey of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">
        The Daily Telegraph
       </a>
      </i>
      described the film as "a paragraph on steroids" that was "neither very terrible nor remotely unexpected. It's a series of stomping footnotes in search of a climax."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">
       BBC
      </a>
      's Nicholas Barber wrote that with the
      <i>
       Hobbit
      </i>
      series Jackson had succeeded in bridging the gap between
      <i>
       The Hobbit
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       The Lord of the Rings
      </i>
      , and that
      <i>
       The Battle of the Five Armies
      </i>
      was a "colossal technical achievement", but he also criticised that the film as such was not compelling because of its repetitive battle scenes and a lack of plot.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nicolas Rapold of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">
        The New York Times
       </a>
      </i>
      said, "Bilbo may fully learn a sense of friendship and duty, and have quite a story to tell, but somewhere along the way, Mr. Jackson loses much of the magic."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
